Been going to this wonderful place since 1988. Classic menu items like ham, roast beef and turkey subs along with speciality items like their chicken club sub. Since I moved out of the area almost 20 years ago my number of visits dropped but still managed to go once or twice every year when I visited the area for work or as a quick stop towards LA to visit family. This time was special since I got to introduce my 18 year old son to the place that many times fed me during my early years in Santa Barbara. My son noticed the Burger items and right away knew what to order. My wife stuck with classic turkey sub with provelon. It's one of her favorites. Glad to see they are ok and doing well during this time of Covid-19. Highly enjoyed my visit and I'm sure you will make the long time favorite list for my son as well.</review>

I have ordered large catering orders at this location multiple times and it is always a hit! The owner is super helpful in helping you figure out how much and what to order based on your headcount. We ended up with a variety of tasty sandwiches for over 80 people and everyone loved them! The best part was we got the exact right amount! I'm very happy with my experience here and will definitely be returning. Thank you!!< /text>

< Text>
First time going to Los Panchos , I asked vegetarian burrito.
The woman working at the time confirmed it was a vegetarian burrito.
Once I was home I obviously bit the burrito a couple times and taste something weird but since I didn't grow up eating pig lard I didn't think anything of it but since it tastes different, I called Los Panchos  and I was told they refry their beans in pig lard.

As a vegetarian I am disgusted that they would do this. Why name something vegetarian and comfirm its vegitarian if it is not.

I have no doubt but their food is probably good since they have good ratings but I just wanted to let the future vegetarians know the BEANS contain PIG LARD.

Vegetarian; a person who does not eat meat, and sometimes other animal products, especially for moral, religious, or health reasons.< /Text>

< text>
HLAY Mother of God.  The food is very unique and the aesthetics of tiki room/jungle hunt is something I'm all in for.  Parking in ktown is a b and painful but this gem is highly recommended.

The Gem lettuce wrap style goat cheese was soo strong for me - the lettuce sizes were perfectly palm sized; there were raisins and apples which I really liked.

Really liked the BEEF TARTARE TOAST - with a bit burnt, smokey toast.  The red chili, scallion, tamari, turnip, kewpie just mixed in together works well.

I almost downed the drink GONE MISSING in one go because it was so refreshingly delicious. Howww is that possible that these flavors all mix so well?  I did not know what was listed in the ingredients but the apricot and pistachio intrigued me.

The SIRLOIN had a surprise mesquite bbq taste - surprised me because I thought it was going to be a regular medium-rare steak.   That baby cut like butter and dipped deliciously with beet bbq sauce

The OCEAN TROUT with orange Julius sauce, hell yes.  With mangos - can't get enough.  Didn't know trout had salmon colors.

The FINGERLING POTATOES - veryyyy crispy on the outside, soft on the inside - very much the way my friend and I like it

And OMG the STRAWBERRY PARFAIT with whipped coconut and frozen, icy, green tarragon complemented the strawberry puree sorbet.  I really want more of this.

LE CRAQUE COOKIE 2.0 with chocolate, walnuts, sesame - what was 1.0?? This was a bit on the too-sweet side but still good, crumbly, chewy, yummy.

I loved that we didn't have to decide what to split for a group of 5 because they portioned everything on the menu for us all to enjoy without worrying about splitting even pieces.  No other restaurant does this and we all appreciated it SO MUCH.  Definitely would come back.

Too much happiness in one sitting.</text>

<rate>5<//rate>< Review>
A restaurant title that sounds like a toast at the end of a comedy central roast episode? you bet I gotta check it out.

Setting: Located in the very busy streets of Los Angeles let me give you a pro tip ***they have their own validated parking lot behind the restaurant that costs $3*** The interior of the restaurant is very trendy that gives off that speakeasy hipster vibe. Old books placed in shelves with lots of interesting artwork and center pieces throughout the restaurant. The seating is very intimate so you'll be hearing your neighbor's conversations

Service: We had a very tall white gentleman who was attentive to us, wait staff was always around to clear the table and refill water glasses when it got half full. Hostesses were very friendly and accommodated our reservation since the LA traffic made us 30 minutes late.

Food: I ordered a deep fried cod ($22) that was flaky and well prepared. I can't say it had the right amount of crisp it kinda had that mushy fishstick texture but regardless i'm easy to please. We primarily came here because of the hamachi kama which was superb. The seasoning tasted like it was the korean red pepper flakes which I wasn't a big fan of and they used it more as a spread on top of the fish rather than  cooking it already seasoned. Nonetheless best hamachi kama I had ever.

Overall: Impress a date and bring them here. Quiet cool ambience, variety of cocktail choices, get to know one another.... or the couple next to you? whichever</Review>

< Text>
I would say 3 1/2 stars, with the potential to go to 4 1/2.
It was my first visit to HLAY and, as expected, I enjoyed the unusual food that this chef creates. We started with the mackerel which came as two separate pieces. It was superb, one of the best preparation of this fish that I have had. Next we enjoyed the heirloom tomatoes as well as the steak tartar. Both dishes were great, although the crispy bits of lap xuong on the tomatoes were too hard and crunchy. Now, both were served in bowls and meant to be shared. This means that you are spooning a portion onto your plate, and, since the ingredients aren't mixed in an even blend, you end up with different flavor profiles.
To me, this is a drawback when a chef creates such interesting dishes. Hence plating them as individual portions would allow more control of how the ingredients are balanced. We concluded with the school shark and the smoked beef tongue. Both were a little one-dimensional in flavor. The shark could have used a little more acidity, a touch of pepper, sea salt, something to offset the mild, slightly sweet taste of its meat. The beef tongue, with its very pronounced smoke flavor could also have benefited from a counterpoint.
We ordered one of their more pricey wine, the Nicolas Badel ‚ÄòIntuition' 2014 syrah ($87). It was disappointing that the bottle was not stored at cellar temperature although I saw a small wine fridge with reds in it. They probably use it for the by-the-glass and less expensive reds because they are ordered more frequently. I found this wine available for $26 in retail, so, if the restaurant marks upwines by a factor of 3.3, then they should find a way to properly store their red wines. It took a while to chill this dense wine  enough so we could drink it. We ordered a glass of red while we waited and it would have been reasonable to have this comped, but it wasn't. Next time I'll probably bring my own wine since the $25 corkage is far more acceptable to me than a 330% markup. That said, the food pricing is pretty reasonable!< /Text>

< review>
This is an OK place to get a few quick items. It's not always possible to do a full grocery run here though, due to the quality of the produce. I've purchased several things only to get home and find out they were expired or bad. For pantry, cleaning and personal care items, the prices are terrific. Also for any type of packaged or frozen food the prices are good. But for very fresh produce and good quality meat, I shop elsewhere. You also will find very limited (if any) quantities of organic produce and meat - weird because the commissary on the south side of base has a good selection.<//review>

< review>
Love this place. I've been coming here for over 15 years and it has never disappointed. It's changed owners once or twice in that time period, but the quality hasn't suffered. Get the #1 Hot Braised Stew Beef Noodle Soup (with tendon), request the fat noodles and thank me later. Not super spicy, but has a solid kick. Bok choy, cilantro, and green onions add great color, texture, and flavor. They don't skimp on the cold side dishes, so be sure to head up to the counter before you order your mains and grab some to munch on while you wait. My personal faves are spicy peanuts, spicy sliced beef stomach, shredded pork ear, and the mustard greens. Pick three from their selection and they'll stack it high on a little plate. I'll be back when I crave that beef noodle.</review>

< Review>
What Happened to Crown and Stache??? I've been going on and off for years - going back to when they were in the Tyler Mall. We took an evening to go and get me out of the house (just had knee surgery - was a bit cabin fevered) and get a nice shave, so C&S it is.
We walked in - all the decor was the same, but the atmosphere was. . . off. Definitely not the C&S we were expecting. Rather than the typical movies or sports, the cosmetologists (you read that right) had taken over the TVs (their words) and put up Disney+ - but not the cool D+, they were watching 30 year old documentaries about Imaginarium (Epcot Center - seriously).
OK, my turn to get into the chair (about 10 minutes late) with the owner. To shave my head and my beard takes me about 30 minutes. . . this took NINETY. FIVE hot towels - why? It's nowhere near as close as I typically get (literally, it's 2 days into where I get it). My mustache is CROOKED (it's noticeably shorter on the right than the left - by about 1/8") and there are several nicks.
The girls were obviously enjoying themselves - laughing about how they got to take over the TVs and watch what they wanted; joking about how since my family was going out of town on Christmas, they "knew which house to break into." (Yes, their words); and how to rip off the local steak-house by going in, pretending to read the menu, and eat all the bread-sticks they wanted (basically dine-n-dash)
What happened? Seriously - from a man-cave serious barber shop, with beer and movies to whatever this place is. It has no pulse, the quality of the cut is low, and the ethics (or bad humor) of the cosmetologists is highly questionable. Me? I won't be back. Ever.</Review>

< text>
The good: The shop is in a nice location and the waiting area is comfortable.  The overall haircut/beard trim was good.

The bad: I went for a buzz cut and beard trim which according to the site should have cost $30, which although on the high side for me was an average price for the type of barber shop it is.  However I was charged $40 which is the price for a haircut/beard trim (although I got a 0 fade up buzz cut). Add to that most of the conversation heard during my time was about how little the barber's made at other shops.

I'll be going back to a shop that's local to my work as I always feel like a valued/appreciated customer there and the barbers attention to detail is great and she does a better job than I received at Crown and Stache.  Add to that she only charges $10 for any time of haircut I request (buzz or otherwise).  Was hoping to find someplace local to my house, Crown and Stache just isn't that place.

I do have to say if I had a kid who was scared of getting a haircut, I probably would spend the extra and take them here for the first couple.</text>

<UserId.>106660356300302376621< /UserId.><name>Casey Helton<//name><Time>1619041618046< /Time><rating>4< /rating>< Text>
We needed to update our two cats' vaccines and Caring Pet Hospital was helpful in getting our appointment setup very quickly. The vaccination process was simple and the doctor who administered them was knowledgeable and kind.
Outside of that though, the place seemed disorganized and gave off a slightly stressful vibe. We're used to going to Chabot Vet Clinic and would highly recommend you go there if they're available. They are much more organized and, well, caring, despite this place's name.
One of the assistants was clearly very unhappy with her job or coworkers and was expressing that under her breath while in the room with us. Not very professional or reassuring.</Text>

< review>
Had to find a vet urgently for a stray cat with some respiratory issues and wasn't able to eat. Caring Pet was the only one able to see us the next day.  I was very pleasantly surprised when the vet did not suggest that full blood work and x-ray. Instead he examined the cat thoroughly, diagnosed a sinus problem, gave it a couple of injections, and sent us home with meds and instructions for a follow-up. The last vet I went to in Castro Valley started well but was churning the cats for $$$, and was not as experienced. I'm somewhat optimistic that I may have found my new vet.< /review>
